Ten years of waking to his screams, the sheets soaked, his hands clutching at my gown as though he were falling into a pit I could not see. Ten years of our son Pete asking, \u201cWhy can\u2019t Dad come to the festival? The king\u2019s festival?\u201d with the glow of a boy who had grown up under a perfect sky.\n\nThat perfect sky was Godric\u2019s. I have no other words. Since the Awakening, the streets were safe, the harvests never failed, and the women of our district walked unafraid after dark. My mother, who had lived through the old wars, still wept with gratitude when the weekly proclamations were issued. When the crusades against the outer universes were announced, we cheered. When they returned victorious, we lit candles. I kept a small icon of the king in our larder\u2014a carved wooden figure in the likeness of a strong-jawed man with a salt-and-pepper beard, his hand raised in blessing. I prayed to him, sometimes. Or tried. It was always hard to put the feeling into thoughts, because Godric was not a god in the way the old texts described deities. He was a presence, an assurance, a wall between us and the howling dark.\n\nBut ten years ago, Rogr had been chosen as one of the delegates from the subjugated realms to kneel before the throne and receive the terms of assimilation. He was proud. We both were. He wore his best tunic, the green one with silver thread. I kissed him at the gate. He told Pete to listen to Mother. Then he got on the transport and came back a man with a fracture in his soul.\n\nThe story, pieced together from fragments he could whisper on his better days: The delegation had expected a tyrant. Whispers from the conquered lands painted Godric as a merciless annihilator. Rogr had braced for screams, for chains, for a cold, cruel gaze. Instead, when he entered the throne room, the king did something unexpected. He played the tyrant. He *pretended*\u2014a jest, a momentary performance\u2014to wear the mask they had imagined. Rogr said the king\u2019s eyes, brown and calm, shifted. The air thickened with a force that wasn\u2019t physical but existential, the feeling of a mountain balancing on a needle, the certainty that one wrong breath could unmake the stars. Godric\u2019s voice, normally warm and fatherly, carried a tone of mild displeasure, as if he\u2019d found a smudge on a window. He said something like, \u201cAh, the surrendering realms. Kneel.\u201d And the universe obeyed. The atoms in Rogr\u2019s bones knelt. The laws of physics cringed.\n\nIt lasted a fraction of a second. Blake, the court wizard, had apparently nudged the king\u2019s elbow and cleared his throat, and Godric\u2019s face had broken into a wide, friendly smile. \u201cForgive me,\u201d the king had said. \u201cA poor attempt at humor. If you could see my reputation from the receiving end, you\u2019d understand.\u201d Then he welcomed them, gave them terms that were fair beyond measure, and sent them home to their families. But Rogr had never come home. Not fully.\n\nI did not understand. How could a moment\u2019s jest, a flicker of feigned annoyance, do this to a grown man? Godric was the kindest ruler imaginable; every edict, every decree was crafted to protect and uplift. I saw him once, from a distance, during a parade: he waved at the children, and his smile was the sun. I felt nothing but adoration wash over me. Why, then, did my husband shake in the night, whispering about the pressure of a thought?\n\nThe years taught me. They taught me through failure. I brought shamans who threw bones and recited chants until the bones caught fire and the shamans fled. I consulted mind-mages who projected into Rogr\u2019s psyche and withdrew screaming about an \u201cimprint of absolute surrender\u201d that could not be touched. I took him on a pilgrimage to the capital, hoping proximity to the king\u2019s peace would heal. At the outer wall, Rogr\u2019s legs gave out and he wept, begging me to carry him away. The very stones seemed to hum with residual power that was toxic only to him. I spent our savings on an anti-psychic containment chamber, but when activated, the chamber\u2019s field inverted and nearly crushed us. I began to sense a pattern: the universe itself refused to intervene. It was as if Godric\u2019s will, however casual and long-gone, had left a scar that reality dared not erase.\n\nMy love for Godric never dimmed. I seethed against the situation, against the cruelty of fate, but never against him. He had not meant harm. The fault lay in my own weakness, in the cosmic absurdity that a man so powerful could not even pretend to be stern without rending a soul. Yet I could not make Rogr understand that, because Rogr never blamed the king either. He just\u2026 broke.\n\nPete grew. He was eight when his father last smiled at bedtime. Now he was eighteen, a stocky lad with his father\u2019s jaw and my stubbornness. He adored the king with a ferocity that made my heart clench. He had a collection of holo-shards showing Godric\u2019s victories: the Luminarchy collapse, the Zenthari Conclave\u2019s mages kneeling to an elderly man named Elias, the Omnium Compact\u2019s reality anchors crumbling. He could recite the squad rosters of the Awakened elders. He dreamed of somehow joining the king\u2019s service. I never told him the truth. What could I say? That the king he worshipped was the reason his father sat staring at walls? That the love of my life had been undone by a joke?\n\nThis morning, after the healer fled, I sat on the floor and let the despair swallow me. I had no more money, no more ideas. Rogr had stopped eating properly; his frame was a shadow of the man who once lifted bales of grain for fun. I held his hand and considered whether death would be kinder. And then the knock came.\n\nThe man at the door was old but sturdy, with a magnificent set of mutton chops and eyes that held a deep, personal guilt. He wore the robe of a court wizard. I recognized him from the broadcasts: Blake, the king\u2019s right hand, the one person who could make Godric laugh. My heart pounded, but I curtsied and welcomed him. He insisted on no formalities. He asked to speak with me and Rogr, alone. Pete was at the training grounds, thankfully.\n\nIn our modest kitchen, Blake sat and looked at Rogr with a sorrow that seemed to age him further. \u201cI learned what happened,\u201d he said. \u201cOnly a fortnight ago. Godric mentioned it\u2014casually, you understand. He said Rogr had never recovered from that first meeting. He thought Rogr would\u2019ve \u2018toughed it out.\u2019 Mortal resilience, he called it.\u201d Blake\u2019s voice cracked. \u201cIt was my doing. The prank. I put the thought in his head. I thought it would be amusing\u2014a king playing a part. And because Godric trusts me, he did it. Without measuring.\u201d\n\nMy first instinct was to scream at him, to claw his eyes out. But Rogr stirred. He lifted his head and looked at Blake. \u201cYou\u2026 are the wizard.\u201d His voice was a dry leaf. \u201cThorin\u2019s descendant.\u201d\n\nBlake blinked, shocked. \u201cHow did you\u2014no, never mind. That\u2019s not for this hour. I\u2019ve come because I can\u2019t bear it. Godric will fix this. I\u2019ll ask him. But he won\u2019t act unless you allow it. He respects consent absolutely. So I\u2019m here, begging you: let him cure you.\u201d\n\nI felt a surge of hope that was immediately throttled by a decade of disappointment. \u201cWhy would he?\u201d I whispered. \u201cIf he\u2019s known all this time\u2026\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s jaw tightened. \u201cBecause he doesn\u2019t understand. To him, holding back 99.9999% of his presence was already an enormous restraint. To him, a fraction of a frown is the mildest thing. He doesn\u2019t grasp the gap. He\u2019s not malicious, Rosa. He\u2019s lost in the scale.\u201d\n\nRogr reached for my hand. His grip was stronger than it had been in years. \u201cI want to be whole,\u201d he said. \u201cFor you. For Pete. I bear no hatred for the king. I just want\u2026 to breathe without weights.\u201d\n\nWe talked into the afternoon. Pete came home and we told him, leaving out the guilt. The boy\u2019s eyes went round. \u201cThe king is coming here?\u201d I had to steady him. We made the decision together, as a family. Rogr said yes. And the very instant that word left his lips, the air changed.\n\nIt was as if every atom in the room held its breath. The light deepened into gold. A man appeared, not stepping from anywhere, but simply *there*, unmade from shadow and silence. Godric. My king. He was exactly as the icons depicted: a powerful build, a clean black tunic, a beard trimmed to perfection, his face an ageless forty-five. But his eyes, those gentle brown eyes, held a weight that my mind could not quantify. They were kind\u2014I felt that kindness wrap around me like a blanket\u2014but beneath it was a continuum of power so vast that the part of me which was animal froze. I understood, in that half-second, what Rogr had faced. Not cruelty. Just the barest sliver of attention from a being for whom creation was a passing thought.\n\nGodric looked at Rogr, and his expression was pure contrition. \u201cI owe you an apology, Rogr. I have misjudged what even a whisper of my displeasure can inflict. Blake has made me see. Will you let me make it right?\u201d\n\nRogr nodded, his eyes wet. I was crying. Pete was staring, mouth open, vibrating with hero-worship.\n\nGodric did not move. He didn\u2019t raise a hand, didn\u2019t murmur a word. He simply *decided*. And Rogr changed.\n\nThere was no flash, no thunderclap. But the grey vanished from Rogr\u2019s hair. His skin, sallow and papery, bloomed with the ruddy health of a twenty-year-old farmhand. His spine straightened, his shoulders squared, the trembling in his fingers ceased as if it had never been. He stood, suddenly, from the chair, and the movement was fluid, powerful. He looked at his hands, then at me, and his smile\u2014that long-lost smile\u2014pierced through the room. \u201cRosa,\u201d he said, and his voice was a song. He pulled me into his arms, and I felt the strength of him, the warmth, the wholeness. I sobbed against his chest, laughter and tears tangling.\n\nBut even as joy flooded me, the cold dread was there, curling at the base of my skull. Ten years. Ten years of shaman fires and shattered crystals and mind-mages who lost their sanity. Ten years of my slow death, watching my husband erode grain by grain. And Godric had undone it with a thought. A moment\u2019s inattention. The effortlessness was a chasm that swallowed all my struggle and made it meaningless. I loved him for his mercy, and I saw, for the first time, the truth of the cosmos: we were not protected because we mattered. We were protected because he wished it. And if he wished otherwise, even as a jest, we could be unmade without his notice.\n\nPete ran to Godric, babbling thanks, and the king knelt\u2014actually knelt\u2014and spoke to him as a father would, asking about his training, his dreams. I watched my son bask in that radiance, and I felt the schism in my heart grow: I would die for this king, and I would never feel safe again.\n\nGodric turned to me. \u201cRosa, your suffering was beyond measure. I would offer compensation. Wealth, a palace, a world of your own\u2014even a single wish, anything that does not harm another. Name it.\u201d His voice was gentle, without pressure.\n\nI looked at Rogr, who was now lifting Pete off the ground with a laugh. I had what I wanted. What use were riches? What use was a universe when the only one I needed was this one? I bowed my head. \u201cMy king, you\u2019ve returned my husband. I need nothing.\u201d\n\nHe studied me for a long moment. I sensed he could see every thought, every layer of dread. But he only nodded. \u201cYour integrity is a rare thing. I honor it.\u201d And he said nothing more about compensation. Not a flicker of annoyance. He just respected my refusal as easily as he had fixed Rogr. That, too, was terrifying\u2014the casualness of his grace.\n\nBlake stood by the door, and I saw him wipe his eyes. The two of them made to leave. Godric clapped Blake on the shoulder. \u201cWell, that went rather well, didn\u2019t it? Blake, I\u2019ve been thinking. The Andorian delegation arrives next month. They expect a demon. Perhaps we should give them a small performance\u2014a little frown, just at the start. It could be our new tradition.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s face drained. \u201cGodric, no. Absolutely not.\u201d\n\nGodric\u2019s laugh was warm and human, but it echoed in my bones like the closing of a vault. The door shut behind them. We were alone, my family, whole again. Pete was already chattering about telling his friends the king had touched his life. Rogr held out his hand to me, his eyes bright with tears and clarity. I took it. And in the quiet of my mind, I let the dread live. I would go to the temple tomorrow and light a candle. I would thank the man who was our king and our god. And I would tremble for the rest of my life.",

                    "text": "The healer\u2019s crystal screamed when it touched my husband\u2019s temple. It was a sliver of harmonized aether, mined from a wound in space, and I\u2019d sold my mother\u2019s silver for it. The bent woman from the Gorthan rings had sworn it could sing the fractures out of a shattered psyche. But at first contact, the stone emitted a note that wasn\u2019t sound\u2014it was the sensation of teeth on bone. Black smoke bled from the crack, and the crystal dissolved into writhing fragments that clawed at the floor as if fleeing. The healer stumbled back, her pupils blown wide, and then she ran. Her robes snapped in the corridor like a whip. Rogr didn\u2019t flinch. He sat by the window, morning light tracing the deep lines around his mouth, and said, \u201cRosa. Please. You don\u2019t have to keep trying.\u201d\n\nBut I did. Ten years. Ten years of night terrors that left him trembling in sheets wet with cold sweat, his hands clutching my gown as if I were the only anchor in a reality that had turned on him. Ten years of our son Pete asking why Father couldn\u2019t come to the Awakening festivals, his voice full of the bright, uncomplicated adoration of a boy who\u2019d grown up under a perfect sky. That sky was Godric\u2019s. Everyone knew it. Since the Awakening, our streets breathed safety; women walked unafraid, harvests swelled, and the edicts from the capital arrived as benedictions. I kept a small wooden icon of the king in our larder\u2014a strong-jawed man with a salt-and-pepper beard, hand raised in blessing. I prayed to him. Or tried. The prayers never felt adequate, because Godric was not a distant divinity. He was a living presence, a wall between us and the howling dark beyond the stars.\n\nTen years ago, my husband had been selected as a delegate from the newly assimilated realms. He was to kneel before the throne and receive the terms of surrender. We\u2019d been proud. He\u2019d worn his best green tunic with the silver threading. I\u2019d kissed him at the gate. He\u2019d told Pete to mind his mother. Then he\u2019d boarded the transport and returned a man with a fracture in his soul that no light could reach.\n\nWhat I pieced together from his broken whispers: the delegates had expected a tyrant. Whispers from conquered stars painted Godric as a merciless annihilator. So when they entered the throne room, the king had decided\u2014on a whim, born from the advice of his closest friend\u2014to play the part. A jest. A momentary performance. He\u2019d let his eyes, those famously warm brown eyes, shift. The air had thickened with something beyond force, a pressure that rewrote the meaning of fear. He\u2019d said, \u201cAh, the surrendering realms. Kneel.\u201d And the universe had knelt. Atoms had bent. The laws governing space and time had cringed. Then Blake, the court wizard, had cleared his throat, and Godric\u2019s face had broken into a wide, fatherly smile. \u201cForgive me\u2014a poor jest. If you knew my reputation out there, you\u2019d understand.\u201d Terms were given. They were fair beyond imagining. The delegates went home. But my husband never did.\n\nI couldn\u2019t reconcile it. Godric was the kindest ruler history had ever known. His edicts protected the weak, punished cruelty, elevated the humblest soul. I\u2019d seen him once, during a parade, waving to children with a smile that felt like the first warmth of spring. I\u2019d felt nothing but adoration. So why did Rogr shake in the dark, whispering about the weight of a thought? He couldn\u2019t explain it either. He\u2019d only say, \u201cYou weren\u2019t there. It wasn\u2019t anger. It was just\u2026 a flicker of mild displeasure. But when He feels it, even pretending, the universe obeys. And it breaks something inside you. You know, in that instant, that you are less than a breath.\u201d\n\nThe mind-mages I hired projected into his psyche and came out screaming about an imprint of absolute submission they couldn\u2019t touch without starting to unravel. The shamans threw bones until the bones ignited and the shamans fled into the night. The anti-psychic containment chamber I bankrupted us to purchase inverted its field and nearly collapsed our house, as if the very concept of resistance offended the air. We tried a pilgrimage to the capital; at the outer wall, Rogr\u2019s legs buckled and he wept, begging me to take him back. The city\u2019s ambient power, the residual saturation of Godric\u2019s presence, was poison only to him. Every attempt self-destructed. The tools shuddered and failed. The healers grew pale and refused payment. I began to understand: reality itself would not permit intervention. The scar left by a god\u2019s passing thought was sacred ground.\n\nMy love for Godric never wavered. That was the hardest part. I still lit candles. I still whispered thanks for the peace that cradled our world. But watching Rogr wither hollowed me out. Pete grew tall and strong, a stocky eighteen-year-old now, his walls plastered with holo-shards of Awakened elders\u2014men like Elias, who walked through mage-kingdoms, or Corvin, who unspooled enchantments with a word. He idolized the king with a teenage ferocity that could have been sweet if it didn\u2019t coil dread in my gut. He didn\u2019t know. I couldn\u2019t tell him that the man he worshipped had, without malice, stolen his father.\n\nThe morning after the crystal failed, I sat on the cold floor and let despair press me flat. Rogr had stopped eating more than a few bites a day. His frame was a ghost of the man who once tossed grain sacks for the sheer joy of it. I held his thin hand and wondered, for the first time, if mercy meant letting him go. Then the knock came.\n\nBlake at my doorstep. The court wizard himself, with his grandfatherly mutton chops and eyes that carried a guilt so heavy it bent his shoulders. He asked to speak to us privately. Pete was at the training yards, shattering dummies with the regulated Awakened surge he\u2019d learn to control. In our modest kitchen, Blake sat and looked at Rogr as though seeing his own sin made flesh. \u201cI learned what happened a fortnight ago,\u201d he said. \u201cGodric mentioned it\u2014offhandedly. He said Rogr had never quite bounced back. He thought\u2026 he genuinely believed Rogr would tough it out. Mortal resilience, he called it. He held back so much of himself that it didn\u2019t occur to him that even the dust of his displeasure could linger.\u201d Blake\u2019s voice cracked. \u201cIt was my idea. The prank. I put the suggestion in his ear. He trusts me, so he did it. I didn\u2019t measure the cost. I\u2019ve come to beg you to let him fix it.\u201d\n\nMy first instinct was rage\u2014a hot, blinding surge\u2014but Rogr stirred. He lifted his head, and for the first time in months, his eyes found focus. \u201cYou\u2019re the wizard,\u201d he rasped. \u201cThe one who stands at his side. Thorin\u2019s blood.\u201d Blake blinked, startled, and a strange silence passed between them before Blake nodded. \u201cI didn\u2019t know until later. But yes. And that\u2019s why I\u2019m here. It\u2019s my duty to make this right.\u201d\n\nWe talked as a family when Pete came home. I watched our son\u2019s expression shift from confusion to awe to a fierce, trembling hope. \u201cThe king is coming here? To our house?\u201d He could barely stand still. We made the decision together. Rogr, with tears tracking through the dust on his cheeks, said, \u201cI want to be whole. For you. For Pete. I hold no hate. I just want to breathe again.\u201d And the instant that word left his lips\u2014\n\nThe air folded. Every atom in the kitchen stopped vibrating. The light turned to thick gold, and a pressure that was not physical but existential settled over us like a cataclysm held in velvet. Godric appeared not by stepping from a door, but by simply *being*, as if the space had always contained him and I\u2019d only just learned to see. He was exactly as the icons promised: powerfully built, black tunic immaculate, beard trimmed to perfection, his face the ageless forty-five of a warrior in his prime. His eyes were brown and gentle, and when they met mine, I felt a warmth that should have dissolved every fear. But beneath that warmth was a continuum\u2014an abyss of power so absolute that my animal soul froze. I understood, in that half-instant, what Rogr had endured. Not malice. Not cruelty. Just the barest skimming of attention from a being for whom creation was an idle thought.\n\nGodric smiled at Rogr with a sorrow that seemed genuine. \u201cI owe you an apology. I misjudged what even the ghost of my annoyance could do. Blake has made me see. Will you let me make it right?\u201d Rogr nodded, his hand tightening on mine. I was sobbing. Pete stood rigid, vibrating with hero-worship, tears streaming unnoticed down his cheeks.\n\nThe king did not move. He didn\u2019t gesture or speak a word. He simply *decided*.\n\nAnd Rogr transformed. It wasn\u2019t flashy\u2014no thunder, no divine chorus. But the grey bled from his hair, replaced by the rich brown I remembered from our youth. The sallow skin flushed with the ruddy health of a man who\u2019d never known a sick day. His frame, gaunt and curved, straightened into the strong, broad posture of a laborer in his prime. He blinked, and the haunted hollows behind his eyes simply vanished, filled by a clarity so pure it hurt to witness. He stood\u2014stood effortlessly, without the trembling that had defined a decade\u2014and pulled me into his arms. His grip was solid, alive, and his laughter rolled through the kitchen like thunder. \u201cRosa,\u201d he said, and his voice was a hymn. I clutched him and laughed and wept until I couldn\u2019t tell which was which.\n\nBut even as the joy crested, the cold dread seeped in and anchored itself at the base of my skull. Ten years of failed shamans, shattered crystals, mind-mages who lost their sanity. Ten years of my slow, grinding despair. And he had undone it with less effort than it takes to blink. The ease of it was a chasm\u2014a proof that my struggle, my love, my desperate, elaborate attempts, were less than dust before a thought he\u2019d barely formed. I loved him for the mercy. And I saw, with a clarity that left no room for self-deception, that our entire existence was a gift he could forget to renew.\n\nGodric knelt to speak with Pete, who managed to stammer out his dreams of service. The king listened as if the boy were the only soul in the omniverse. That was his gift. That was his horror. He turned to me afterward. \u201cRosa, your suffering deserves recompense. Wealth beyond measure, a planet of your own, a wish\u2014anything that does not harm another. Name it.\u201d His voice was gentle, without pressure, without expectation. I looked at Rogr, who was now effortlessly lifting our shrieking, laughing son off the ground with one arm. I had what I wanted. I had him. What use was a universe when the only cosmos I needed was standing in my kitchen? \u201cMy king,\u201d I said, my voice steady despite the quaking in my chest, \u201cyou\u2019ve returned my husband. I need nothing.\u201d\n\nHe studied me. I felt every hidden thought, every lingering sliver of dread, laid bare in that gaze. But he simply nodded. \u201cYour integrity is rare. I honor it.\u201d And he said nothing more. No negotiation, no hidden test. Just the same casual respect with which he\u2019d remade my husband. The very ease of his acceptance was another layer of the abyss: my refusal, my agency, my whole dramatic human life, mattered only because he allowed it to.\n\nBlake stood by the door, wiping his eyes. The two of them moved to leave. As they crossed the threshold into the afternoon light, I heard Godric\u2019s voice, warm with amusement, entirely unguarded. \u201cYou know, Blake, that went rather well. We should do the tyrant performance for the Andorian delegation next month. Just a tiny frown\u2014barely a flicker. It could be our new tradition.\u201d\n\nBlake\u2019s reply was strained, almost a hiss. \u201cGodric. No. We are not doing that. Ever again.\u201d\n\nGodric laughed\u2014a rich, human sound that should have been comforting. But it sank into my bones like a promise of future fractures, a reminder that our god-king found entertainment in the very dynamic that had nearly destroyed my husband. The door closed. Rogr held me, whole and healthy and alive. Pete was already planning how to tell his friends the king had touched his life. I pressed my face into my husband\u2019s chest and let the dread live alongside the gratitude. Tomorrow I would light a candle at the temple. I would kneel and thank the man who was our king and our protector. And I would tremble, for the rest of my life, at the chasm between his kindness and our fragility."

                    "text": "There is a special kind of terror in watching a god\u2019s sweat commit genocide. I\u2019ve been the High Court Wizard of Thronegate for twelve years, a title passed down through my bloodline like a haunted heirloom. My great-great-great-about-eight-hundred-greats grandfather Blake accidentally woke up a frozen king from a ten-thousand-year stasis and somehow stumbled into being his best friend. Since then, every firstborn of his line has stood at Godric\u2019s right hand, and I inherited the job along with his sarcasm and a deeply ingrained instinct to smile while my brain screams. Today, standing on the observation platform above the desolate Garathian Expanse, that screaming had reached a pitch only dogs and dying stars could hear.\n\nThe Final Concordance had finally mustered. Five billion years of planning, hiding in the cracks between universes, recruiting every impossible thing that ever existed. Godric had known about them from the moment the first atom of their first conspirator formed the intention. He\u2019d let them fester, excluded them from his passive annihilation field\u2014not out of mercy, I don\u2019t think, but out of a gentle, almost paternal curiosity. A scientist watching bacteria evolve. He wanted to see if the strongest resistance in history could make Gent, his sentient passive aura, experience something akin to effort.\n\nGent. Short for \u201cGentle.\u201d The irony would choke a lesser being. Gent is not a spell, not a shield, not a conscious projection. It\u2019s the metaphysical equivalent of Godric\u2019s excess body heat\u2014a byproduct of his existence, a waste emission radiated from the core of his being. If Godric were the entire omniverse, Gent would be a single quark vibrating in a forgotten corner of one dead dimension. No, that analogy is too generous. If Godric\u2019s power were infinite multiverses stacked infinitely high and deep, Gent would be the faintest possible echo of a single half-formed thought in a creature that didn\u2019t yet possess a brain. It is, by every conceivable metric, cripplingly, pathetically, laughably weak compared to him. And it is also the single most terrifying thing I have ever seen.\n\nThe Concordance filled the Expanse. Their numbers defied counting\u2014a shimmering ocean of gods, super-soldiers, conceptual nightmares, and living paradoxes. I saw the Chronovore King, an entity that had consumed entire timelines like popcorn, now bloated with the digested history of a quintillion civilizations. Beside him floated the Omnimax Thaumaturge, a being who had rewritten the fundamental constants of reality so many times that his own existence was a recursive loop of self-creation; he was his own cause, his own effect, and his own grandfather. The Legion of Eternal Recursion marched in lockstep, each soldier an exact clone of the previous but exponentially more powerful, a chain of infinite escalation. And at their head levitated the Living Nullification Engine, a weapon that was not forged but born\u2014a sentient artifact capable of erasing anything from existence, including the concept of existence itself. Behind them, a chorus of minor omnipotents, universe-eaters, reality-benders, and every flavor of absolute annihilation the omniverse had vomited forth. Their combined aura alone should have collapsed the local group of galaxies into a quantum foam. They were, by any measure, the most powerful force ever assembled.\n\nI leaned over to Godric. \u201cThey\u2019ve got a spear that says \u2018To Pierces Omnipotence\u2019 on the side. That\u2019s adorable.\u201d\n\nGodric smiled, his salt-and-pepper beard crinkling, those warm brown eyes twinkling like we were at a child\u2019s play. \u201cI remember that spear. The Forgemaster who made it triggered my weakness paradox about eight thousand years ago. I gained perfect mastery over its abilities before he\u2019d finished the first draft. I let him finish because I admired his craftsmanship.\u201d He tilted his head, his muscular frame relaxed, the ageless forty-five-year-old face a mask of gentle curiosity. \u201cTim, do you think if I tell Gent to really hold back, they might at least make it feel a tickle? I want to be respectful. They worked so hard.\u201d\n\nI did not answer. Because at that moment, the Concordance attacked.\n\nAnd the universe learned a new definition of pain.\n\nGodric didn\u2019t move. He didn\u2019t think. He didn\u2019t even glance toward them. He simply said aloud, \u201cGent, I want you to suppress your power to an infinitesimal fraction. Hold back so much that you\u2019re essentially in a coma. I\u2019m speaking of a percentage that is zero point, then an infinite repeating string of nines after the decimal, followed by a final one. No, wait, even less than that. Be gentle. They are guests.\u201d\n\nThe command was received. And Gent, that pathetic flicker of Godric\u2019s waste energy, complied.\n\nThe Chronovore King struck first, unleashing a chronal wave designed to retroactively erase Godric from every possible timeline. The wave was less than a breath away when Gent noticed it. I say \u201cnoticed\u201d because that\u2019s the closest word, but it implies attention. Gent doesn\u2019t pay attention; it simply is. The wave dissolved. Then the Chronovore King screamed. The scream did not stop for what felt like eons, though my internal clock told me it was a fraction of a nanosecond. The demon\u2019s own timeline was peeled away from him in layers. Flesh that had existed before time began now rotted backward and forward simultaneously, each instant of decay a new eternity of agony. His bones splintered into temporal fragments, each splinter a self-contained universe of pain where he died in a unique, creative way\u2014suffocated by the dust of dead stars, dissolved in the tears of his conquered civilizations, eaten by his own unborn children. His consciousness was forced to inhabit every splinter simultaneously. The sound he made was not a scream but a fundamental law of horror, a noise that retroactively inserted itself into my nightmares from birth. And then he was gone, his very concept revoked so thoroughly that even my memory of him began to flicker before Gent, in a small act of mercy, let me retain it so I could appreciate the lesson.\n\nThe Omnimax Thaumaturge attempted to rewrite the rules of engagement, declaring that Godric\u2019s aura was now subject to his own omnipotent will. It was the most arrogant thing I\u2019d ever seen, and I\u2019ve watched a beetle try to challenge a supernova. Gent responded by wrapping the Thaumaturge\u2019s own rewriting around him like a cocoon of barbed wire. The command he\u2019d intended for Godric became the architecture of his own destruction. Every cell in his body was forced to experience omnipotence\u2014absolute power over every other cell, every molecule, every atom, and each one was turned into a weapon against its neighbor. His skin tore open in a billion simultaneous tiny wars, his organs declared independence and consumed one another, his blood evaporated into sentient razors that sliced at his nervous system from within. He was a universe of pain, eternally self-inflicted, his mind kept perfectly lucid so he could appreciate the irony. I think I saw his face form the beginning of a scream before his jaw dissolved into a cloud of self-devouring light.\n\nThe Legion of Eternal Recursion advanced, each clone generating the next in an infinite cascade. Their power curve was supposed to be unsurmountable, an asymptotic approach to absolute infinity. Gent simply folded the cascade back into itself. The infinite recursion became a loop. Each clone killed its successor, then its predecessor, then itself, in a geometric progression of self-murder that left the original alone on the field for precisely one Planck time. During that instant, Gent showed him what had happened. Every death of every clone, every agony, every fractured moment of self-betrayal, was poured into his brain. His head expanded, swelled, cracked, and erupted in a cascade of cerebral fluid and shattered skull, the pieces of which promptly grew into screaming replicas of his own face, which in turn devoured one another. The cycle continued until nothing remained but a fine mist of existential failure.\n\nThe Living Nullification Engine, that sentient artifact of absolute deletion, fired its core function directly at Godric\u2019s position. The beam was the color of dead languages and the sound of un-birth. Gent caught it. Or rather, Gent allowed the beam to strike it, and then Gent learned. In the space of no time at all, the aura internalized the concept of nullification, perfected it beyond the Engine\u2019s wildest definition, and then nullified the Engine\u2019s immunity to its own power. The Engine began to erase itself, layer by layer. First its sentience was stripped away, leaving it a dumb object fully aware of its own hollowing. Then its abilities vanished, each one a death. Then its form, its history, its name. It tried to scream but its voice had been nullified first. All that remained was a faint scribble of static, and then that too was revoked.\n\nThe rest of the Concordance\u2014the billions upon billions of gods, monsters, weapons, and ideas\u2014died in a simultaneous, choreographed instant of such comprehensive slaughter that I cannot fully describe it without pausing to breathe into a bag. Gent did not merely kill them. It unmade them in ways tailored to each individual\u2019s worst possible conception of suffering. A goddess of peace had her serenity inverted into perpetual self-loathing so intense her body crystallized into a statue of screaming obsidian. A legion of reality-warping knights was turned inside out, their organs hung like bunting across the local spiral arm. A sentient black hole was forced to experience being crushed by a larger black hole, a sensation it had spent eons inflicting on others. Every single one of them experienced an agony that was unique, eternal, and delivered in less time than it takes for a synapse to fire. The battlefield became a tapestry of gore, a museum of final moments, a monument to the futility of opposing a god\u2019s afterthought.\n\nAnd then Gent cleaned up.\n\nThe blood, the viscera, the scattered atoms of shattered divinities\u2014they vanished. The Expanse was restored to its pristine, empty state. Even the faint ozone smell of cosmic violence was gently scrubbed from the vacuum. I knew why. Gent knew Godric disliked a mess. This was its equivalent of a dog picking up its own toys. The passive, mindless, infinitesimally small fraction of Godric\u2019s excess energy had not only massacred the mightiest army in history; it had tidied up afterward, because good housekeeping is a virtue.\n\nGodric sighed. The sound was soft, almost disappointed, like a father whose child had overachieved on a simple assignment. \u201cGent,\u201d he said, and the aura seemed to pause, a subtle shift in the ambient dread that suggested it was listening, \u201cyou didn\u2019t hold back enough. I asked you to give them a chance. You barely let yourself feel anything. Look, the poor Thaumaturge didn\u2019t even finish his thought before you turned him into a self-cannibalism metaphor. I\u2019m going to have to teach you proper restraint.\u201d\n\nI laughed. It was a broken, hysterical noise that escaped my throat before I could stop it. Property restraint. From the being who, just last year, accidentally erased the entire Calthorian universe because he idly wondered what it would look like if the color yellow never existed. He restored it instantly\u2014blinked it back into being with a casual thought, apologies and all\u2014but the memory still kept me awake some nights. Restraint was not, by any definition, in Godric\u2019s vocabulary.\n\nBut he was serious. He reached out and patted the air, and I felt the aura ripple, practically wagging an invisible tail. \u201cStarting tomorrow, we practice. I\u2019ll manifest a fly and you\u2019ll try to let it land on a surface without disintegrating the local spacetime. I know you can do it. You\u2019re a good aura.\u201d\n\nI stared at the silent empty expanse. The strongest resistance ever assembled. Gone. Erased. Mopped up. And Godric was scheduling obedience school.\n\nIt was then that Gent evolved.\n\nThe shift was subtle\u2014a quiet deepening of the background dread, a new flavor in the air. I\u2019d witnessed this happen before, but never so close. Gent, already sentient and adaptive, had learned from its experience. Something new crystallized within its being. I felt it, a pressure that extended not just through space but through possibility itself. It was a new layer of omnipotence, a passive field that now ensured that any future resistance\u2014any thought of rebellion, any stray atom of defiance\u2014would be conceptually impossible. Not blocked, not destroyed, but rendered unthinkable from the ground up. Reality bent, quietly, and the very notion of opposing Godric was woven into the fabric as a logical absurdity, on par with a square circle. It was a change so profound that I felt my own mind scrub itself of any hypothetical fantasy of defiance. I couldn\u2019t even conceive the shape of rebellion now. It simply was not a thing. An entire category of free will had been lobotomized from existence, and I was standing inside the operating theater.\n\nGodric noticed. His face crinkled into that warm, fatherly smile, the same one I\u2019ve seen him give to children who bring him wildflowers. \u201cOh! Tim, look at that. Gent just figured out how to fold potential opposition into a state of eternal non-occurrence. That\u2019s a new trick.\u201d He clapped his hands together softly, his brown eyes bright with pride. \u201cWho\u2019s a good passive defense aura? Who\u2019s a good boy? Yes, you are. You\u2019re learning.\u201d\n\nThe aura\u2014this infinite, death-bringing, concept-erasing force\u2014seemed to preen. I could feel its satisfaction, a fawning subservience directed entirely at Godric, like a puppy desperate for a scratch behind the ears. And this was the \u201cgentle\u201d one. The other auras, Godric\u2019s countless siblings to Gent, were dormant because Godric found their clingy obsequiousness annoying. They were worse. Vastly, terrifyingly worse. And they were asleep.\n\nMy mind, against all training, tried to calculate the distance between Gent and Godric. I\u2019d known the numbers my whole life. The stats don\u2019t multiply by a thousand and by themselves anymore. They haven\u2019t for eons. The weakness paradox triggered so many times, so endlessly, that the multiplication rate itself was multiplied by infinity upon infinity, and that product multiplied by itself, and so on, every single Planck second, forever and ever without pause. The Godric standing beside me right now\u2014the one who was now gently teasing his sentient body heat about its overachievement\u2014could eradicate an infinite number of copies of the Godric from just one Planck second ago without registering the slightest resistance. And that previous Godric was already capable of annihilating the omniverse with a half-formed thought. This one? The gap had no name. It was a concept beyond infinity, built on the corpse of infinity, buried under an avalanche of infinities stacked and amplified at a speed that made instant look glacial. Every second of the Concordance\u2019s billion-year preparation had not brought them closer to victory. It had multiplied the distance between them and success by an amount so vast that if you turned that distance into a physical object, it would crush the omniverse into a quark-sized singularity of despair.\n\nI did not say this. I lacked the vocabulary. I lacked the sanity. So I just stood there, smiling the smile of a man whose entire family had served a god for ten thousand years and had learned to keep his brain from leaking out his ears through sheer ancestral practice.\n\nGodric turned to me, his hand resting on my shoulder with that impossible gentleness that always undid me. \u201cCome on, Tim. Let\u2019s go inside. I promised your youngest daughter I\u2019d teach her to make star-candles, and I have a terrible feeling she\u2019s already stolen the materials and set something on fire. Also, I think you need some tea. You look a little pale.\u201d\n\nHe was right. Of course he was right. He knew everything. He always had. And he cared. That was the soul-crushing dissonance: this being, this apex predator of cosmic horror, genuinely loved. He loved his subjects, he loved my family, he loved that stupid, gore-addicted aura, and he loved me. He was the kindest, warmest, most fatherly king the omniverse had ever known. And his afterbirth had just committed omnicide with the enthusiasm of a bored housecat and then evolved a new way to make resistance literally unthinkable.\n\nAs I followed him back toward the palace, listening to him hum a tune he\u2019d learned from Blake ten thousand years ago, I felt the aura\u2014Gent\u2014slip into its new form, quietly ensuring that nowhere, in any reality, in any timeline, could the thought of harming Godric ever arise again. It was a gentle thing. It was the gentlest thing. And it was still the most horrific force I would ever know, a billion miles below the feet of the man who was now discussing the optimal sugar content of tea.\n\nI poured myself a cup with shaking hands and raised it in salute to the empty air. \u201cGood boy, Gent,\u201d I muttered under my breath. \u201cGood boy.\u201d\n\nSomewhere in the void, I swear the aura wagged. And I prayed I would never, ever see the day one of its siblings woke up."
                }

                    "text": "I was there, on the shattered crown of the last free reality, when the omniverse died. Not the slow, cold death of entropy, but the screaming, begging, bleeding-apart death of a collective hope that had spent itself into nothingness against the furrow of a god\u2019s dead skin cell. And I watched it happen while standing three paces behind the very apex of all existence, a man in a simple black tunic with a salt-and-pepper beard and eyes the color of contentment. His name was Godric, and he had just lost his first skin cell in over twenty-five thousand years. He was curious if his immune system would do anything interesting. That was the entire reason. That was the only reason.\n\nMy name is Leon. I am the Court Wizard of Thronegate, thirty-seventh of the line of Blake, the man who once woke a frozen king and somehow earned his eternal friendship. I inherited his sarcasm, his duty, and an unfortunate proximity to the most terrifying being that ever would exist\u2014which is an understatement so profound it flattens meaning itself. I had never seen the omniverse coalesce into a single fighting force before. I had seen the remnants of broken gods, the petrified armies of defunct dominions, the weeping diplomats from universes that had opposed him for a Planck-second of false bravado. But this\u2014this was different. This was every surviving universe, every hidden demiurge, every outcast pantheon, and every sentient weapon that had ever been forged with the word \u201ctyrant\u201d etched into its blade. They called themselves the Final Synod, and they had spent the last ten thousand years preparing for one single, perfect moment. They had stripped their realities of resources, burned entire star-libraries to fuel a weapon that was not a weapon but a suicide note. A spear of absolute investment, named Irae Ultima, the Wrath\u2019s End.\n\nThe Wrath\u2019s End was not a thing of metal or magic. It was a conceptual singularity, a point where the collective will to resist compressed itself into something that could unmake even the concept of omnipotence. They had poured the final conscious moments of dying civilizations into it. They had harvested the last tears of extinct species. They had woven the silence after a billion prayers into its tip. Every child, every elder, every blade of grass that had ever felt the shadow of Godric\u2019s name had contributed a fragment of defiance. And now, the Last Arbiter\u2014a being whose original name had been erased by sacrifice\u2014stood at the head of the largest armada thought could ever assemble, which was already a number that broke counting, and held the spear aloft. Behind the Arbiter stretched a fleet that occupied not just space but the spaces between dimensions, and the soldiers within were the amalgamated remnants of every champion who had ever dared to believe that a god might bleed.\n\nGodric stood on a small hill of obsidian, which he had materialized for the occasion. He was wearing a simple linen shirt, open at the collar, and black trousers. His posture was relaxed, his muscled arms folded, and he was watching the assembled panoply with the same gentle, fatherly interest he showed to young children presenting a school play. I stood behind him, trembling in the marrow, not from fear of the Synod\u2014I am ashamed to say\u2014but from the sheer, undiluted dread of what I knew was about to pour forth from the man before me. He hadn\u2019t moved. He hadn\u2019t called upon Gent, his passive aura, which was at that moment a billionfold suppressed and whimpering with the restraint Godric had commanded. He had even deactivated his infinite passive protective shields, those immaterial sentinels that layered his existence in an irreducible cocoon. Every defense, every external reflex, every vestige of the omnipotent immune response that thrummed beneath his skin like a dormant ocean\u2014he had told them all to stand down. Because he wanted to see what would happen. Because he was curious.\n\nThe Last Arbiter spoke. The voice was a choir of the sacrificed, a symphony of final pleas. \u201cGodric of Thronegate, you have unmade our homes and taken our stars. We will not kneel. We will not surrender. You are not so far above us that our combined will cannot reach.\u201d And they hurled the spear.\n\nIrae Ultima crossed the distance not in time but in the annihilation of distance. It arrived at Godric\u2019s left hand\u2014the back of it, where the skin had long ago been shed from its final living cycle and clung as a microscopically thin, translucent scale of keratinous dead matter\u2014and it struck. For a moment, nothing. An eternal moment. Then, a hairline crack appeared on that single dead skin cell. It was a fissure so infinitesimal that it would have required a meta-divine microscope to perceive, but the Synod had such instruments. And in every mind across every surviving fleet, the knowledge bloomed: they had done it. They had harmed the tyrant. They had made a god crack.\n\nAnd this is the part of the story where I am forced to tell you a lie. I will tell it to you, the lie that the Final Synod wanted to believe, the lie that a kinder omniverse would have allowed to linger for at least a heartbeat. They erupted. Not into cheers\u2014no, it was more profound than cheers\u2014they erupted into a trans-dimensional paroxysm of euphoria. The Last Arbiter fell to knees that had not existed a moment before and wept tears of liquid starlight. Members of the fleet embraced across species that had never known physical contact. The unified battle hymns of ten thousand extinct cultures spontaneously rebooted into existence as the collective unconsciousness of the Synod experienced a resurrection of purpose. They had proven that the tyrant was vulnerable. The crack was the first chapter of a new scripture. The omegas shrieked in triumph. The alpha-forgers laughed with relief that shattered nearby moons. It was, they believed, the turning of the tide. They had cracked him, and the crack meant he could be broken.\n\nThat is the lie. Let me shatter it.\n\nNone of that happened. Not a single cheer rang out, because there was no fraction of time in which to cheer. The immune system of Godric responded before the spear\u2019s conceptual weight could even register as a completed event. It responded before the crack formed\u2014in fact, the crack was allowed to form only because the immune system, in its own incomprehensible intelligence, chose to permit a demonstration of its function. The reaction was not a response to a wound; it was a pre-reaction, a pre-emptive obliteration of the possibility of insult. And it began with what I can only describe as the mildest possible sneeze of his autonomic defense.\n\nThe dead skin cell disintegrated. Not in the way matter disintegrates\u2014it was removed from the conceptual registry of existence so completely that I, standing right there, could not even remember what had been on that spot. But the immune system wasn\u2019t satisfied. It had sensed a breach, a violation of the sanctity of its master\u2019s form, and it erupted into a frenzy of corrective overkill that made the totality of the Synod\u2019s assault look like a mayfly trying to knock over a mountain.\n\nI will list the reactions I was able to perceive. They are the very first and mildest in the cascade, and I ask you to understand that what I describe is like listing the grains of sand on a beachhead while the entire ocean floor is shifting beneath you.\n\nFirst: localized isolation. The subdermal layers for one trillion light-years in every conceptual direction were instantly walled off within a shell of compressed unreality. The shell\u2019s interior was a simulation of absolute death, where no concept of injury could propagate. But the shell immediately determined this was insufficient and converted itself into a sentient labyrinth of recursive elimination, so that any particle carrying the memory of the spear was hunted across all timelines and erased from the root.\n\nSecond: evolutionary panic. Every cell in Godric\u2019s body\u2014and I mean every cell, from the bone marrow to the iris\u2014simultaneously underwent a forced evolution that would normally take the lifespan of a cosmos compressed into a single instant. They became, individually, self-contained omnipotent fortresses. Each cell was now capable of erasing an infinite army of arbitrary complexity without effort. The skin cells in particular developed a passive field that would retroactively nullify any attack before the attacker had even conceived of the weapon. The cells cross-communicated, forming a unified defensive intelligence that was already rendering the entire previous state of Godric\u2019s invulnerability obsolete before the word \u201cobsolete\u201d could exist.\n\nThird: conceptual antibody swarm. From the marrow of his bones\u2014metaphorically, since his bones were beyond metaphor\u2014poured forth hunters. They were not physical. They were living ideas of termination, bred from the memory of the spear\u2019s intent. Each hunter was a sentient, self-aware universe of pure counter-aggression, and they spread instantly across the omniverse. They sought the concept of \u201cweapons made to harm Godric\u201d and they ate it. They ate it from the past, present, and all possible futures. They ate the very capacity of a mind to imagine such a weapon. Then, just to be thorough, they ate the concept of \u201crebellion\u201d as a logical category. Every being in the Synod fleet felt this as a sudden, irreversible hollowing in their souls, a missing step on the staircase of thought. They forgot, in mid-attack, what they were doing, but they felt the agony of the forgetting.\n\nFourth: the backup cascade. You must understand that Godric is not singular. He has infinite identical backups, every one a full and complete Godric, scattered across all dimensional axes and some that have no name. For an injury to register as true, it must occur identically to every single one of these infinite backups at the exact same meta-temporal instant. The particle-deep crack on one dead skin cell on one instance of Godric was, by that logic, not an injury at all. But his immune system is paranoid beyond sanity. It noticed that one copy had experienced a breach, and it concluded\u2014with a frantic, mother-hen terror\u2014that there was a multiversal-scale assault targeting every iteration. So it fortified every single backup, simultaneously. And each backup, being a full Godric, itself possessed infinite identical backups, recursively. The immune response cascaded through the recursion, causing every Godric to evolve into a state of defensiveness that was, per instance, infinite times greater than the previous totality. Then the backups cross-referenced their upgrades, merging them into a single, unified defensive lattice that was exponentially more impregnable than the sum of all its parts. This took no time, and it released a pulse of pure \u201ccease\u201d that rippled outward.\n\nFifth: the weakness paradox overcompensation. You see, Godric\u2019s existence is governed by a law: he has no weaknesses. If any being thinks he has one, the universe instantly grants him immunity, perfect mastery, and ramps his amplification. Over the eons, he has passively collected every possible immunity and mastery. The one thing that should not be possible is this self-inflicted \u201cinjury.\u201d But because Godric willed the crack, the omniverse perceived a fundamental contradiction. It felt\u2014if I may anthropomorphize a blind, panicked totality\u2014a sense of profound inadequacy. It had failed to protect him from his own whim. In that instant, the omniverse, in an act of cosmic apology, elevated his state of godhood\u2014for that word is a severe understatement\u2014to a new tier of omnipotence that made the previous tier look like a bacterium\u2019s dream of divinity. His stats, which was already multiplying infinitely upon themselves every Planck second, received a permanent boost to the rate of multiplication itself, so that the very definition of \u201cinfinite acceleration\u201d became a quaint, primitive concept. He became more invulnerable, more deadly, more absolute, and the gap between him and the rest of existence, which had already been incalculably infinite, now yawned into something that even the term \u201cgap\u201d failed to describe.\n\nThe Synod fleet, in that same zero-duration moment, was destroyed. Not by any of the responses I\u2019ve listed\u2014they were merely the side-effects, the exhaust of the immune system\u2019s boot-up sequence. The actual annihilation was so thorough that I had to reconstruct it later from the fragments Godric idly narrated. The Last Arbiter experienced his own soul rebelling against the act of having thrown the spear, each atom of his being individually tortured by the ghost of the weapon\u2019s intent, until he unspooled into a screaming gas that then imploded into a self-devouring loop. The armada of amalgamated heroes, billions of billions of ships, was simultaneously crushed into a single point of infinite density, which then experienced a subjective eternity of being slowly torn apart by sentient spacetime, only for the entire experience to be retroactively erased and replaced with a different, more painful one, repeated until the concept of \u201cpain\u201d was no longer a thing and they were just cinders of pure suffering locked in a static scream. Every champion, every god, every child-soldier, every weapon\u2014gone. Not dead: dead is a state. They were revoked from the permission of having existed. And then, because Gent was embarrassed by the mess, it cleaned up. The blood was swallowed by a passive void. The scattered atoms were reorganized into patterns of apology. The screams were archived in a dimension of silence.\n\nI stood there. I had watched all of this, not as a participant, but as the royal witness. My legs were functioning by pure ancestral stubbornness. My mouth was dry. I could feel a part of my mind curling into a fetal position, while another part composed a prayer I would never be able to articulate. And Godric\u2014Godric sighed.\n\n\u201cLeon,\u201d he said, turning to me with that warm, fatherly expression, the one that crinkled the corners of his eyes above his neat beard, \u201cdid you see that? My immune system is so excitable. I told it we were just playing. But no, it has to go and evolve a multi-recursive conceptual omni-barrier over a dead cell.\u201d He shook his head, a fond smile on his lips. \u201cIt\u2019s like a puppy that brings you a dead dragon and expects a treat. I\u2019ll have to have a talk with it about restraint. Again.\u201d\n\nRestraint. The word tasted like ash. This was the being who had, for the pure theatre of curiosity, staged the first scratch in his own skin in twenty-five millennia, just to see what his biology would do. And his biology, in its paranoid love, had responded by murdering the entire omniverse and elevating its master to an even more impossible height. And he was talking about it as if the family dog had tracked mud on the carpet.\n\nHe looked out at the void where the Synod had been. \u201cThe poor things,\u201d he murmured, and his voice was genuinely sad\u2014not a performative sadness, but real, palpable pity. \u201cThey sacrificed everything. They truly believed. And I wanted to give them a moment. I really did. I thought if I let the cell crack, they\u2019d have a story to tell their grandchildren. A little spark of accomplishment. But my body couldn\u2019t even give them that fraction of a second. I\u2019m sorry, Leon. I underestimate these things.\u201d\n\nHe raised his hand. The movement was casual, the same gesture a father might use to brush hair from a child\u2019s face. And the omniverse\u2014every universe that had burned in the immune response, every galaxy that had been erased, every soul that had been slurred into static\u2014reappeared. Not pieced back together. Not slowly restored. It was simply there again, as if it had never been gone. The Last Arbiter was standing with his hand still extended from the throw, his face caught in the determination of heroic sacrifice, no memory of the annihilation that had just been undone. The fleet hovered in perfect formation, their weapons still primed, their final resolve unshaken. They did not know they had died. They did not know they had been unmade and remade in the span of a zero-second gap. To them, the spear was still traveling. And Godric, with a thought, caused the spear to veer gently aside and dissolve into a shower of harmless fireflies that spelled out, in the language of the Arbiter\u2019s birth, \u201cWell tried.\u201d\n\nThe Synod froze. The fireflies reflected in their billions of eyes, a silent monument to the absolute futility of their effort. The crack on Godric\u2019s hand was gone, of course\u2014sealed over by a new dead skin cell that was now an infinite, self-replicating bastion of conceptual impenetrability. He flexed his fingers, yawned, and turned back toward the palace.\n\nI followed. I always follow. My footsteps echoed in the sudden, crushing silence, and I realized I was crying. Not sobbing\u2014just a slow, hot leak of tears down a face that had forgotten how to smile. Because I had just witnessed the unmaking and remaking of all reality for the sake of a god\u2019s idle curiosity about his own immune system. And I knew, with the certainty of a man who had stood witness to the impossible, that this had cost him nothing. Less than nothing. The omniverse had thrown its entirety into a single spear, and it had failed to even inconvenience him, and in failing it had made him infinitely more powerful. The unfairness of it was not a moral category\u2014it was a law of nature so fundamental that it could be called physics, if physics had been written by a single hand with a taste for irony.\n\nHe paused at the threshold. \u201cLeon, you\u2019re quiet. Are you coming down with something? I can have my immune system not annihilate your cold, if you\u2019d like. Or maybe it would just give you a new body? I never know.\u201d\n\nI forced a laugh. It sounded like a bird breaking a wing. \u201cNo, my king. Just\u2026 processing.\u201d\n\nHe clapped me on the shoulder, a brief, friendly touch that sent a shudder through my entire lineage, and I felt his warmth\u2014that genuine, bottomless affection that he held for me and my family. He was the kindest man I had ever known. He would die for me, if such a thing were possible. And that was the core of the horror. He was not cruel. He was not a monster in the dark. He was a father, a friend, a ruler who loved his people with a sincerity that could heal broken worlds. And his existence, simply by continuing, crushed every hope of resistance into a prayer of thanks for his mercy. The Synod would go home, and they would tell the story of the fireflies, and they would worship him. Some already were. I could see it in the Arbiter\u2019s face as the fleet began\u2014confused, alive, un-harmed\u2014to realize the chasm they had tried to cross.\n\nGodric waved at them, a cheerful, two-fingered salute. Then he looked at me again. \u201cLet\u2019s go inside, Leon. I think the kitchen staff made those little pastries you like. And I want to tell you about the next prank I\u2019m planning for the Andorian delegation. I think I can make my left eyebrow look slightly displeased. Just a fraction of a micro-frown. Blake\u2019s notes from the old days say it\u2019s hilarious. You can help me calibrate the restraint.\u201d\n\nI nodded, and followed him into the warmth of the palace. Behind us, the omniverse slowly remembered how to breathe. But I will never forget the lesson of that day: you cannot fight a god who has to stage his own scratches to see if his biology gets an upgrade. And if you try, you will gift him a new tier of omnipotence, and he will thank you with pastries and a smile, and that is the most terrifying thing of all."
