                    "text": "The throne room of Thronegate smelled of old cedar and fresh bread. Godric liked the kitchens close. He said the smell of yeast reminded him of something\u2014a morning long before the stasis, when his wife Reina had baked a cake for their youngest. He\u2019d told me that story on my first day as Court Wizard, and I\u2019d stood there, twenty-two years old, clutching a staff I barely understood, listening to the most powerful being in creation reminisce about a burnt pie crust. That was Godric. That was the man who could unmake the omniverse with less effort than it takes to sigh, and who chose instead to sit in a modest chair wearing a linen tunic, asking if I\u2019d had breakfast. Three years later, I\u2019d learned that the warmth wasn\u2019t a mask. It was genuine, and that made the abyss behind it infinitely worse.\n\nMy name is Grim. I am the thirty-ninth Court Wizard of Thronegate, a direct descendant of Blake, the merchant who pulled Godric from the ruins and taught him how to laugh again. I inherited this job, the staff of gnarled oak, and a hereditary case of internal screaming that I\u2019d learned to swallow with a smile. At twenty-five, I was the youngest Court Wizard in our history, and I\u2019d already witnessed enough cosmic erasures to know that the friendly salt-and-pepper beard and the fatherly pat on the shoulder were the gentlest chains ever forged around a mind.\n\nThe envoy came on a day thick with spring pollen. His name was Xeraxis, and he represented the Velari Ascendancy, a pocket-universe civilization that had somehow evaded Thronegate\u2019s expansion for fifty millennia. They hadn\u2019t surrendered. They hadn\u2019t fought. They\u2019d sent a diplomat, thinking they could do what armies could not. I\u2019d scanned the reports: the Velari were a race of psionic intellects, evolved from crystalline hive-minds that had spent eons debating the nature of reality until they\u2019d learned to manipulate it with sheer argumentation. They\u2019d once out-negotiated a black hole into releasing its captured light, or so the legend went. They thought they were clever.\n\nGodric had been looking forward to the meeting. \u201cA new flavor of arrogance,\u201d he\u2019d said over breakfast, slicing an apple with the same hands that had once accidentally willed a star cluster into nonexistence and then brought it back with an embarrassed apology. \u201cI\u2019ve been hoping for something fresh. So many of them just recycle the old ones\u2014\u2019I have a hidden army,\u2019 \u2018This weapon can unmake gods,\u2019 \u2018Look at my conceptual nullification orb.\u2019 It gets tedious.\u201d He\u2019d looked at me, his brown eyes bright with a curiosity that I knew, with the cold certainty of a man who\u2019d seen the truth, was entirely performative. He already knew what Xeraxis would do, what he would say, the precise tremor in his telepathic voice when his plan collapsed. He knew everything, always. He just liked to let the story play out.\n\nXeraxis entered with the confident stride of a creature who believed in the power of a well-turned phrase. His body was a lattice of shifting quartz and captured starlight, twelve feet tall, his consciousness projecting a telepathic hum that translated into the air as a faint musical chime. I felt the pressure of his psionic scrutiny brush against my mind\u2014cautious, arrogant, already cataloguing me as a tool he could manipulate. He didn\u2019t try to read Godric. He was too smart for that. He thought.\n\n\u201cKing Godric of Thronegate, I bring the regards of the Eternal Conclave of Velari,\u201d he intoned, his voice like wind through glass tubes. \u201cWe have watched your march across the skies with awe. We know the futility of martial resistance. Therefore, we offer a proposal of enlightened union\u2014a compact that binds neither party in servitude, but in mutual prosperity. We wish to join your dominion as equals, not subjects.\u201d\n\nHe produced a scroll. It unfurled in the air, and its surface shivered with a script that wasn\u2019t entirely visible\u2014layers of magical encoding buried under layers of subtext, the kind of contract that would take a mortal wizard a thousand years to parse. I caught a whiff of binding magic, something oath-level, but subtly woven. My hand tightened on my staff. Before I could speak, Godric patted my arm gently. \u201cWait, Grim. Let the man present his gift.\u201d\n\nThe king\u2019s eyes never left Xeraxis, but they were softened with that grandfatherly indulgence he showed to children who built castles in the sand. He leaned back in his chair\u2014not a throne, a simple wooden chair\u2014and crossed his muscular arms, the image of a relaxed, aging patriarch who had never quite shed his soldier\u2019s build. His salt-and-pepper hair was cropped short, his beard neatly trimmed, and his smile could have belonged to any friendly merchant in the capital markets. Xeraxis almost smirked. I saw the flicker in his psionic aura: he was thinking he\u2019d already won.\n\n\u201cThe compact is simple,\u201d Xeraxis continued. \u201cIt establishes a perpetual trade of knowledge, a mutual defense clause, and a cultural exchange that will enrich both our peoples. In return for Thronegate\u2019s protection, we offer Velari\u2019s deepest secret: the Gnostra Protocol, a method of extracting infinite computation from a single thought. We\u2019ve heard that you value innovation, King Godric.\u201d\n\nI knew then. I knew this was a trap. The Velari were known for their contractual cunning, their ability to hide clauses within clauses, to bind gods through the sheer nuance of linguistic recursion. The Gnostra Protocol was a myth, a lure. The real contract, buried in the subtextual folds, probably contained a clause that would transfer sovereignty to the Velari, or limit Godric\u2019s power, or bind his will to their decisions. It might even be a conceptual weapon aimed at his omniscience. But as I opened my mouth, Godric held up a finger, and I went silent.\n\n\u201cLet me have a look,\u201d Godric said. He lifted a hand toward the floating scroll, and the gesture was so casual\u2014the same way a man might reach for a newspaper. Then he did something I\u2019d never seen him do. He read it.\n\nNow, understand what \u201creading\u201d means for Godric. He possesses absolute omniscience. He didn\u2019t need to look at the scroll; he\u2019d known every character of its script before the Velari first conceived of writing, before their universe was even a twitch in the cosmic womb. But he held it, and his eyes tracked across the lines, and his lips moved slightly, as if sounding out words. He was playing along. The performance was so thoroughly perfect that, for a heartbeat, I almost believed he was genuinely examining it.\n\nThen he smiled wider. \u201cOh, this is lovely. It\u2019s beautifully layered. There\u2019s a triple-encrypted sub-clause in paragraph twelve that redefines \u2018mutual defense\u2019 as \u2018Thronegate forces under Velari command,\u2019 isn\u2019t there? And a recursive oath-loop in appendix nine that would, if I sign, bind my will to the Conclave\u2019s collective consciousness, effectively making me a figurehead. Plus a hidden conceptual trigger that would rewrite my memory of ever consenting to the hidden parts. Very thorough.\u201d He chuckled, a genuine, grandfatherly chuckle. \u201cI haven\u2019t seen a recursive oath-loop in... oh, it must be forty thousand years. Last one was from a cabal of temporal deities who tried to sue me for existential damages. Nice people.\u201d\n\nThe air in the room didn\u2019t change. The light didn\u2019t dim. But Xeraxis\u2019s crystalline form flickered\u2014a stochastic shudder that betrayed a psionic mind reeling. His telepathic hum lost its musical edge. \u201cYou... you cannot have read that. The subtextual folds are keyed to a cipher only the Conclave\u2019s highest minds can perceive. You\u2019d need a cognitive substrate infinite times more complex than\u2014\u201d\n\n\u201cThan the omniverse?\u201d Godric finished. He set the scroll down. \u201cLet me save you the trouble, Envoy. I\u2019ve been aware of the Velari Ascendancy\u2019s plans since the moment the first atom in your universe formed the potential for thought. I knew what you\u2019d say before you were born. I knew the exact phrasing of your opening remarks twelve thousand years ago, when your species was still evolving the vocal cords it would never need. And I knew, as I smiled and asked your envoy to sit, that you\u2019d brought a contract designed to enslave me.\u201d He tapped the scroll with a finger. The parchment quivered. \u201cI was curious. It\u2019s a rare pleasure to see a new draft of the old hubris. But it\u2019s still just a variation. I was hoping you\u2019d surprise me.\u201d\n\nXeraxis recoiled. His crystalline form tried to phase-shift\u2014a teleportation reflex\u2014but the room held him. He wasn\u2019t going anywhere unless Godric allowed it. The panic I saw then was a thing to witness: the slow cracking of a mind that had never, in eons of existence, encountered a problem it couldn\u2019t solve with words. His telepathic voice splintered into a dozen frequencies. \u201cYou cannot blame us for trying. You are a tyrant. You crush all who resist. We sought only to preserve ourselves.\u201d\n\n\u201cA tyrant?\u201d Godric placed a hand over his heart, the gesture of a man deeply, sincerely wounded. \u201cI offered you unconditional surrender a thousand years ago. You refused. I offered it again five hundred years ago. You refused. I\u2019ve never attacked the Velari Ascendancy. I\u2019ve let you build your schemes, because I believe in letting children play with their blocks before they have to go to bed. But you didn\u2019t come here to surrender. You came here to win.\u201d He leaned forward, his voice dropping to a hush that was still warm, still kind, and now infinitely more terrifying than any roar. \u201cSo let me show you what winning looks like.\u201d\n\nAnd then, for just a fraction of a second, Godric allowed himself to be understood. Not in his fullness\u2014the omniverse would shatter if he did that\u2014but in the shallowest, most infinitesimal sliver of his actual cognitive architecture. He let Xeraxis see a single thought. A single, passive, idle musing, the kind that floated through Godric\u2019s mind a thousand times in every Planck instant. I didn\u2019t see it directly, but I saw Xeraxis see it, and that was enough.\n\nThe envoy\u2019s crystalline body didn\u2019t break. It unspooled. The lattice of quartz and starlight became a screaming fog, and that fog was forced, by the sheer weight of revelation, into a shape that could still perceive. I couldn\u2019t tell you the content of that thought, but I could read its effect. Xeraxis began to recite, without volition, every deception he\u2019d ever conceived, every hidden plan the Conclave had ever drafted, every scheme, every betrayal, every cynical manipulation he\u2019d perpetrated across the long centuries of his life. His telepathic voice became a ceaseless torrent of confession, and with each word, his form grew more ragged, more fragmented, as if truth itself was pulping him from within.\n\nAnd still Godric sat, that gentle smile on his face, like a father who\u2019d caught a child in a lie and was patiently waiting for the apology.\n\n\u201cI used the Treaty of Seraph\u2019s Light to sell my own brother into servitude for a seat on the Conclave,\u201d Xeraxis sobbed, because his voice could still sob. \u201cI fed misinformation to the Krell ambassadors to start a war that would exhaust their energy reserves. I let my daughter believe she had surpassed me so she would lower her guard and I could absorb her innovations.\u201d On and on it went, every sin, every cruelty, every clever thing he\u2019d once called victory. And Godric listened, his head tilted, his expression one of faint sorrow\u2014not cruelty, not satisfaction, just the mild disappointment of a man who\u2019d hoped the cookie jar would be empty but had found a half-eaten smuggled stash instead.\n\nThen the thought ended. Xeraxis collapsed, his form reassembling into a diminished, half-opaque crystal shape. He was still alive, still conscious, but something fundamental had been stripped away. His arrogance, perhaps. His belief in his own intelligence. The contract he\u2019d brought\u2014the Binding Compact of Mutual Prosperity\u2014crumpled into dust and reassembled itself, rewritten by a passive flicker of Godric\u2019s will, into a simple instrument of unconditional surrender, already signed with Xeraxis\u2019s own psychic signature.\n\n\u201cThere,\u201d Godric said. \u201cThat\u2019s fair. You wanted a compact. Now you have one. The Velari Ascendancy is a territory of Thronegate, effective immediately. You\u2019ll be given the Awakening at a reduced magnitude\u2014just tenfold per year, like our own citizens. I\u2019m not cruel.\u201d He looked at me. \u201cGrim, would you see the envoy to his transport? He\u2019s had a long morning.\u201d\n\nI moved on autopilot, my legs hollow. Xeraxis stumbled beside me, his crystalline hum now a faint, broken whistle. As we walked the long corridor to the outer gate, he turned to me, and the eyes that formed on his surface were wet with the alien equivalent of tears. \u201cHow?\u201d he whispered. \u201cHow do you stand beside that? Seeing what I saw\u2014how do you not go mad?\u201d\n\nI thought about it. I really did. For fifty thousand years, my lineage had stood at Godric\u2019s right hand. We\u2019d watched him obliterate resistances, erase threats, heal traumas, and bake pies. We\u2019d lived in the shadow of a being whose every passing thought could unmake us, and we\u2019d learned a truth that Xeraxis, for all his intellect, had yet to grasp. I put a hand on his shuddering shoulder. \u201cHe\u2019s not mean,\u201d I said. \u201cThat\u2019s the part that breaks you. He genuinely loves. He cares about his people, about my family, about the smallest flower that dares to bloom. And he is, simultaneously, the most terrifying thing that ever will exist. You don\u2019t reconcile those facts. You just learn to breathe around them. You\u2019ll learn, too. It\u2019s the only way to survive the warmth.\u201d\n\nAfter the envoy left, I returned to Godric. He was standing by the window, looking out at the city. The sun was setting, painting the spires in shades of amber and rose. He turned when I entered, and his face broke into that warm, fatherly smile. \u201cYou look pale, Grim. I hope that wasn\u2019t too much. I was trying to hold back. I really only showed him the barest outline of a half-formed notion\u2014like a single brushstroke from a painting the size of the universe. But I forget sometimes. Mortal minds are delicate.\u201d He patted my shoulder, and the weight of his hand was the weight of creation. \u201cI\u2019m proud of you. You\u2019re good at what you do.\u201d\n\nI managed a nod. I knew, without him saying, that he could see every thought in my head. That he\u2019d seen my reflection on the corridor, my silent reckoning with the chasm between his kindness and his capability. That he saw everything, always, and that he chose, in his infinite wisdom, not to mention it. Because there was a wisdom beyond intelligence, and his had concluded, eons ago, that the scariest thing he could do was to be a simple, friendly old father. For his people, that was enough. For me, the boy who\u2019d inherited a legacy of witnessing infinity in a smile, it was the daily bread of existential dread. But I would eat it, and I would thank him, and I would stand at his right hand until my own death, because no one else could. And because somewhere, deep in the unending recursion of his knowledge, he counted me as a friend.\n\nAs I walked out to the gardens to calm my nerves, I heard him speak to the empty air. \u201cSee, Gent? You didn\u2019t have to intervene. Sometimes just showing them a little piece works better. You could learn from that.\u201d The air shimmered in reply, a submissive wagging of a metaphysical tail. I kept walking, and the terror followed me like a loyal pet, never biting, never leaving. That was Thronegate. That was home."

Gorm insists on protecting Godric. They encounter a magical entity born from the universe's dying curse, something of immense power. Gorm attacks, but his best spell is nothing. Perhaps when Godric unmakes the entity, Gorm's magical senses, amplified by his awakening, catch a glimpse of the sheer infinite depth of Godric's magical reservoir, a sea that makes the multiverse a droplet. He collapses in awe and horror.\n\nAfterward, Gorm is catatonic for a while, then starts to function but with a hollow understanding. He now knows that Godric is the source of all magic, or at least infinitely above it. But we must not say Godric invented magic; prompt says not to claim Godric invented magic because Thorin was already a wizard before stasis. So Godric's magic is just one aspect of his omnipotence.\n\nThe story should be in Gorm's voice, first person. He'll recount the events leading to his shattered belief.\n\nLet's draft an outline:\n\n- Opening: Gorm's pride as a newly appointed court wizard at 20. He is the youngest to hold the post (maybe others died or retired). He has trained all his life in the arcane arts, believing it's his sacred duty to protect King Godric, who he sees as a kind but magically defenseless uncle. He talks about family: his father was the previous court wizard, and so on. He mentions the Awakening: all male Thronegate citizens gain 10x power per day past 20, but his line gets a special thousandfold boost (though Godric never said why). He attributes his impressive magic to his bloodline and the intense training.\n\n- Scene: In the palace, Gorm is checking wards around Godric's quarters. Godric enters, and they have a warm, friendly chat. Godric calls him \"my boy\" and ruffles his hair. Gorm feels protective.\n\n- Inciting event: A diplomatic ceremony with representatives from a far-off universe that recently surrendered. During the ceremony, a magical assassination attempt occurs\u2014an enchanted artifact that summons a dimensional rift to swallow the king. Gorm is the only wizard present besides Godric, and he leaps into action, casting a banishment spell of immense power (his own creation). But before his spell can impact the rift, Godric raises an eyebrow. The rift freezes. Not just freezes, but the very concept of the assassination attempt is retroactively erased\u2014the artifact disappears, the summoning fails, and the representatives are left blinking in confusion, their memories cleaned. Gorm, with his heightened magical perception, catches a fleeting afterimage of what Godric did: a tiny, involuntary pulse of magic from Godric that not only nullified the attack but rebuilt the local reality to ensure it never occurred. The pulse was so minuscule that it was like the gravitational effect of a single quark at the edge of the omniverse. But to Gorm's senses, it was a tidal wave of absolute omnipotence that made his most powerful spell look like a child's sparkler. He experiences a moment of utter cosmic horror as his mind tries to comprehend the scale: the pulse he witnessed was not even a conscious act; it was Godric's magic's passive reflex, a yawn of his arcane metabolism. Gorm's understanding of magic is shattered.\n\n- Aftermath: The ceremony concludes. Gorm is pale, trembling, unable to speak. Godric notices but says nothing about the event, instead asking if Gorm is hungry. The cognitive dissonance drives Gorm deeper. Back in his quarters, he weeps, not from sadness but from the existential dread of realizing that his entire life's purpose is a fantasy, that the being he serves could unmake all magic with a fleeting thought. He realizes that all the Awakening power he has is a gift from Godric, that Godric's concealment was a mercy to let them feel useful, and that the true nature of the universe is that there is an infinite, bottomless power that cares for them like pets. He now understands why the court wizard lineage has always been filled with cheerful, humble people\u2014they all eventually learned this, and they coped by embracing the absurdity. But Gorm is still reeling.\n\n- He goes to speak with Godric, but finds he cannot articulate his terror. Godric, with omniscience, simply says, \"You did well today, Gorm. I'm proud of you. Your spell was creative. Don't lose that spark.\" The words, meant as comfort, twist the knife: Godric is praising his uselessness. Gorm smiles and nods, his internal world a silent scream.\n\n- The story ends with Gorm standing in his tower, looking out at the peaceful capital, feeling the weight of an unassailable god's love pressing down on him, knowing that he will serve until death, and that his magic will never matter. The horror lingers.\n\nWe need to exaggerate the magic gap: \"an infinitesimal fraction of Godric's magic can instantly and effortlessly erase an entire omniverse infinite times over.\" So I'll describe Gorm's perception: when he witnesses that pulse, he sees that within Godric, there is an ocean of magic so vast that each cell in his body contains an infinite magical potential that dwarfs the multiverse. The pulse he saw was the equivalent of a single skin cell flaking off, and even that was infinitely more than all magic ever cast in all existence.\n\nWe must also mention the infinite Planick-second multiplication; that his magical aptitude is infinitely increasing, so what Gorm saw is already infinitely obsolete. That's a layer of horror.\n\nAlso, the weakness paradox: Godric has all magical masteries, etc. But not needed too much.\n\nI'll write the story as Gorm's first-person account, using his voice: a young, earnest, dedicated wizard, then broken. The tone should be dark, oppressive.\n\nNow, let's craft the narrative in prose.\n\nWe'll open with a scene that establishes Gorm's confidence and love for Godric.\n\nThen transition to the key event.\n\nUse sensory details: the smell of ozone in the ceremony hall, the feel of his staff, the taste of iron in his mouth when the revelation hits.\n\nAftermath: his inner monologue, the silent despair.\n\nMake sure no warm ending: the last lines should be unsettling, like \"I smiled back, because that was my job, and because the alternative was to scream until the stars went out, and even then He would hear me.\"\n\nI need to avoid explicit moralizing, but just present the horror.\n\nLet's begin writing.",

                    "type": "text",
                    "text": "The hall of the Veltaran Surrender was dressed in the usual pageantry: banners of crimson and black, the sigil of Thronegate\u2014a closed fist cradled by an open palm\u2014hanging limply from the rafters. I stood one step behind the king, my new court wizard robes still stiff at the collar, my staff humming with primed wards. At twenty years old, I was the youngest to hold the post in four centuries, a fact that made my father beam at the ceremony and my mother weep into her embroidery. I accepted the honor with the solemn confidence of a young man who had been told, since the day he first conjured a spark, that his bloodline carried a sacred duty: to protect the king with the arcane.\n\nI called him Uncle Godric. I\u2019d known him since I was small enough to ride on his shoulders through the garden, plucking luminescent peaches from the orchard. He was a big man, broad-shouldered and barrel-chested, with a salt-and-pepper beard that I\u2019d watched him trim with a small silver knife since before I understood what he was king of. He smelled of old books and baking bread, and he had a laugh that could make the chandeliers tremble. I knew, as everyone knows, that Godric was powerful\u2014that he had crushed the old galaxy\u2019s mightiest armies, that his rule now spanned the omniverse. But I, in my youthful arrogance, had constructed a neat little syllogism: the king is unstoppable in war, the king is a strategic genius, the king does not cast spells; therefore, the king needs a wizard. I was that wizard.\n\nThe Veltarans had surrendered without bloodshed three weeks prior, a peaceful annexation after a century of stubborn independence. Their delegate, a spindly creature of braided light and chitin, knelt before the throne and offered the customary oath. The words were a formality; Godric received them with a warm nod, his brown eyes crinkling at the corners. He wore a simple black tunic, no armor, no crown. He looked like a retired soldier who had wandered into the wrong ceremony. I remember thinking, as I scanned the crowd for hidden threats, that if an assassin struck, it would be my moment. My father had told me once, over a campfire during a training trip to the Outer Rings, that a court wizard\u2019s purpose was to be the one thing the king could not be. \u201cWe stand in the gap, Gorm, between mortality and the void. And if the void ever looks our king\u2019s way, we fill that gap with everything we have.\u201d\n\nI was thinking about that, the warm pride of it, when the void looked our king\u2019s way.\n\nIt came from the delegate\u2019s own ceremonial scepter\u2014a trap buried under layers of treaty-oath magic, a sacrificial last gasp from a faction of Veltaran hardliners who had spent decades forging a weapon out of dying stars and impossible mathematics. The scepter split open and vomited forth a rift. Not a simple tear in space, but a sentient, hungering wound designed to sever its target from the topology of existence, to unwrite the concept of a person so absolutely that the omniverse itself would forget the shape of them. I perceived it with my mage-senses as a shriek in eleven dimensions, a cascade of un-becoming that had been tailored specifically for an omnipotent signature.\n\nMy body moved before my mind. A shield erupted from my staff, layered with counterspells I\u2019d been honing since adolescence\u2014a lattice of paradox absorption, ontological grounding, and a recursive locking weave that should, by every measure of arcane theory, stall even a conceptual weapon. I poured every ounce of my amplified power into it. My bloodline, you see, is special. All Thronegate men receive the Awakening upon turning twenty: for every day we live past that age, our physical and mental attributes increase tenfold. But my family\u2014the direct descendants of Blake, the king\u2019s oldest friend\u2014we receive a thousandfold increase each day. At twenty years old, I had only just begun that climb, but my training and my birthright made me, I believed, one of the most potent wizards alive. My shield could have tanked a supernova. I was so certain.\n\nThe rift touched my shield and ignored it. Not broke through\u2014ignored, as a man ignores a soap bubble. I felt the feedback like a snap of cold wire across my brain, the total and immediate failure of everything I had built. The rift lunged for Godric.\n\nAnd then Godric flicked a glance at it.\n\nNot a glare. Not a word of power. He just looked at it, the way a man might glance at a fly buzzing near his lunch, and the rift stopped. But it was more than stopping. My mage-senses, still raw and wide open from the shield\u2019s collapse, buckled under the weight of what I perceived next. I will try to tell it, though language is a blunt tool and what I saw was a scalpel of infinite sharpness.\n\nThe rift was not countered. It was not dispelled. The concept of its existence was gently, absentmindedly lifted from the fabric of reality and folded inward until there was no longer an \u201cit\u201d to reference. But the source of that folding\u2014that was the horror. Underneath Godric\u2019s warm, fatherly exterior, there lay a magic so vast that my mage-senses ceased to function as senses at all and became a direct pipeline of terror to my soul. I perceived it as a single, minute pulse\u2014like the heat shed from a skin cell flaking off a body that dwarfed eternity.\n\nThat pulse, less than a stray thought, less than a half-formed idle curiosity, contained magical energy sufficient to erase not merely the rift, not merely the army that forged it, not merely the entire Veltaran universe, but the entire omniverse\u2014every dimension, every timeline, every layer of existence stacked from the first mote of chaos to the final silence\u2014a trillion times over, and that would still be the gentlest, softest exhalation of his least active cell. I saw, in that instant, that Godric was not a man who lacked magic. He was the absolute apex of all arcana, a reservoir of such abyssal profundity that the total sum of all spells ever cast by all wizards across all ages was less than a single atom in a sea that had no shores. And his magic, this ocean of impossible omnipotence, was multiplying. Not merely growing, but recursively, infinitely reinforcing itself every Planck second\u2014its rate of increase already so far beyond the concept of infinity that my mind could not even brush against the idea without shorting out\u2014and that meant that the negligible pulse I had just witnessed was, in the instant following my perception, already quaint and obsolete compared to the new baseline of his being.\n\nThe delegate, the court, the entire assembly never noticed. The rift was gone; the ceremony continued. Godric smiled and accepted the now-ordinary scepter as if the Veltarans had offered him a particularly interesting spice jar. \u201cA lovely design,\u201d he said, turning it over in his hands. \u201cI\u2019ll put it in the gallery. Grim\u2014are you all right? You\u2019ve gone pale.\u201d\n\nI tried to answer. My throat had turned to sand. He looked at me with those warm, caring eyes, and I saw, behind them, the faintest shadow of that vastness\u2014not a threat, not a display, just the passive truth of his existence that his immense will normally suppressed into a charming human shape. He had held back so thoroughly that for twenty years I had thought of him as the smiling uncle who needed a wizard. The lie was not his; it was the mercy he extended to all of us, a concealment so perfect that we could pretend we mattered in the way we wanted to matter.\n\nI don\u2019t remember much of the rest of the ceremony. I stood at my post, my legs trembling under my robe, and I did not cast a single further spell because no spell could ever matter again. I was a man who had just learned that the fortress he\u2019d sworn to guard was itself the foundation of all reality, that the king he\u2019d vowed to protect could unmake the concept of protection with a yawn. I was a firefly circling a black hole, and I had just glimpsed the event horizon.\n\nThat night, in my tower, I wept. Not tears of grief\u2014there was no one to mourn\u2014but the physical overflow of an existential dread so complete it had no other exit. I sat on the cold stone floor, my staff across my knees, and I replayed the moment over and over. The pulse. The abyss. The cheerful way Godric had later clapped me on the shoulder and said, \u201cYou really gave it your all, Grim. That shield had a clever retrograde cascade. I remember your great-great-grandfather tried something similar during the Klendathu Uprising. You have his spark.\u201d His spark. My spark was a cinder, and his was the furnace of creation.\n\nIn the days that followed, I moved through the palace like a ghost. I performed my duties\u2014checking wards that were as necessary as a paper umbrella in a typhoon\u2014and I learned to smile when Godric called me \u201cmy boy.\u201d I learned to converse about trivial things while my brain screamed the same silent scream. I began to understand why my father always had a faint air of detachment, a look in his eyes that I had mistaken for sage calm. It was not calm. It was the permanent, low-grade horror of knowing that your entire purpose was a prosthetic limb for a being who had no body to lose.\n\nOne afternoon, as I stood near the throne room watching Godric explain the rules of a board game to a child from the city, I realized something that broke the last strut of my sanity. He knew. He had always known. He knew my boyish confidence, my proud little shield, my secret thought that I was the essential guardian of an unguarded king. And he had let me believe it\u2014not out of cruelty, but out of a kindness so absolute that it tipped into the most profound humiliation. He had given me my purpose because I needed one, and he had ended it with the gentlest possible apocalypse, leaving me to reconstruct myself from the ashes of my own insignificance. I could not even resent him for it. He was not mean. He was the best thing that had ever happened to the omniverse. He was the tyrant who loved, the predator who sheltered, the annihilation that coddled. And I had been foolish enough to think he needed my magic.\n\nThat evening, as the sun set over the capital spires, I was alone in the western observatory when a familiar warmth settled beside me. Godric had not walked in; he was simply there, an option the universe had quietly accepted. He looked out at the sky, his profile the same eternal forty-five, and said nothing for a long while. The air hummed with the weight of unspoken truths. Finally, he laid a hand on my shoulder, and I felt, through that touch, the absolute restraint required to not vaporize me with his mere presence.\n\n\u201cGorm,\u201d he said, and his voice was the same honeyed tone he\u2019d used when I was five and had scraped my knee. \u201cYou don\u2019t have to keep the wards up. They\u2019re pretty, but they\u2019re unnecessary. I just like seeing what you create. It reminds me of your ancestor.\u201d\n\nI couldn\u2019t answer. I just nodded, a tight, jerky motion. He patted me once and was gone. The terror remained, a new organ in my chest that beat in time with my heart. I had no closure, no resolution. There was only the unending truth: I was a wizard to a god who had no use for magic except as a love letter to his dead friends. And I would serve him until I died, and my magic would grow a thousandfold every day, and it would never\u2014never\u2014be anything but a speck. That was my inheritance, and I carried it silently, the way my father had, and my grandfather before him, a lineage of court jesters whose jokes were spells and whose king had infinite patience for the punchline."
